<div id="videocontainer" style="padding-bottom:10px;margin: 0 auto;min-width: 400px;width: 50vh;max-width: 700px;"></div><h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Victory Road (Kanto)</h1><div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"><div id="siteSub">From Bulbapedia, the community-driven Pokémon encyclopedia.</div><div id="contentSub" dir="ltr" lang="en"></div><div id="jump-to-nav"></div><a href="#column-one" class="mw-jump-link">Jump to navigation</a><a href="#searchInput" class="mw-jump-link">Jump to search</a><div id="mw-content-text" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><table style="float:right; background: #A66A42; width: 30%; margin-left: 10px; margin-bottom: 10px; border-radius: 10px; -moz-border-radius: 10px; -webkit-border-radius: 10px; -khtml-border-radius: 10px; -icab-border-radius: 10px; -o-border-radius: 10px; border: 2px solid #E0B192;">

</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Victory Road</b> (Japanese: <b>チャンピオンロード</b> <i>Champion Road</i>) is a tunnel situated on <a href="/wiki/Kanto_Route_23" title="Kanto Route 23">Route 23</a>. It earned its name because it must be traveled by all <a href="/wiki/Pok%C3%A9mon_Trainer" title="Pokémon Trainer">Trainers</a> aiming for the top. Its other end opens up in <a href="/wiki/Indigo_Plateau" title="Indigo Plateau">Indigo Plateau</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pok%C3%A9mon_League" title="Pokémon League">Pokémon League</a>. Only Trainers with the eight <a href="/wiki/Kanto" title="Kanto">Kanto</a> or <a href="/wiki/Johto" title="Johto">Johto</a> <a href="/wiki/Badge" title="Badge">Badges</a> are allowed to enter it.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_the_games">In the games</span></h2>
<p>Victory Road has three floors. To reach the other end of the tunnel in <a href="/wiki/Generation_I" title="Generation I">Generations I</a>, <a href="/wiki/Generation_III" title="Generation III">III</a>, <a href="/wiki/Generation_IV" title="Generation IV">IV</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Generation_VII" title="Generation VII">VII</a>, a series of puzzles involving using <a href="/wiki/Strength_(move)" title="Strength (move)">Strength</a> or <a href="/wiki/Secret_Technique" title="Secret Technique">Strong Push</a> to move <a href="/wiki/Movable_boulder" title="Movable boulder">boulders</a> need to be solved.
</p><p>In Generation I and <a href="/wiki/Pok%C3%A9mon:_Let%27s_Go,_Pikachu!_and_Let%27s_Go,_Eevee!" title="Pokémon: Let's Go, Pikachu! and Let's Go, Eevee!">Pokémon: Let's Go, Pikachu! and Let's Go, Eevee!</a>, Victory Road is where the <a href="/wiki/Legendary_Pok%C3%A9mon" title="Legendary Pokémon">Legendary Pokémon</a> <a href="/wiki/Moltres_(Pok%C3%A9mon)" title="Moltres (Pokémon)">Moltres</a> can be found. In <a href="/wiki/Pok%C3%A9mon_FireRed_and_LeafGreen_Versions" title="Pokémon FireRed and LeafGreen Versions">Pokémon FireRed and LeafGreen</a>, it is instead found at <a href="/wiki/One_Island" title="One Island">One Island</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Mt._Ember" title="Mt. Ember">Mt. Ember</a> and is subsequently found in <a href="/wiki/Mt._Silver" title="Mt. Silver">Mt. Silver</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pok%C3%A9mon_HeartGold_and_SoulSilver_Versions" title="Pokémon HeartGold and SoulSilver Versions">Pokémon HeartGold and SoulSilver</a>.
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Move_Tutor" title="Move Tutor">Move Tutor</a> at the very end of Victory Road in Pokémon FireRed and LeafGreen offers to teach a Pokémon the <a href="/wiki/Move" title="Move">move</a> <a href="/wiki/Double-Edge_(move)" title="Double-Edge (move)">Double-Edge</a>.
</p><p>In Pokémon: Let's Go, Pikachu! and Let's Go, Eevee!, an <a href="/wiki/Officer_Jenny" title="Officer Jenny">Officer Jenny</a> is present of 2F, healing the <a href="/wiki/Player_character" title="Player character">player</a>'s Pokémon if talked to.
</p><p>In some promotional artwork for <a href="/wiki/Generation_II" title="Generation II">Generation II</a>, Victory Road is depicted as being part of Mt. Silver, but this is not confirmed.
</p><p>In Generations II and <a href="/wiki/Generation_IV" title="Generation IV">IV</a>, there are no Trainers in Victory Road. According to <a href="/wiki/Silver_(game)" title="Silver (game)">Silver</a> in Pokémon HeartGold and SoulSilver, the reason for this is because he defeated them all.
</p><p>In Pokémon HeartGold and SoulSilver, after entering the <a href="/wiki/Hall_of_Fame" title="Hall of Fame">Hall of Fame</a> and boarding the <a href="/wiki/S.S._Aqua" title="S.S. Aqua">S.S. Aqua</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pok%C3%A9mon_battle" title="Pokémon battle">battle</a> music in Victory Road (as well as in the <a href="/wiki/Tohjo_Falls" title="Tohjo Falls">Tohjo Falls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kanto_Route_26" title="Kanto Route 26">Routes 26</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kanto_Route_27" title="Kanto Route 27">27</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kanto_Route_28" title="Kanto Route 28">28</a>) changes from the Johto style to the Kanto style. This change was not present in Generation II.
</p>

</p><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Generation_II">Generation II</span></h4>
<p><i>In the Japanese and Korean games, <a href="/wiki/Ursaring_(Pok%C3%A9mon)" title="Ursaring (Pokémon)">Ursaring</a> appears only in Silver, while <a href="/wiki/Donphan_(Pok%C3%A9mon)" title="Donphan (Pokémon)">Donphan</a> appears only in Gold.</i>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_the_anime">In the anime</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Victory_Road_PO.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//archives.bulbagarden.net/media/upload/thumb/0/0c/Victory_Road_PO.png/250px-Victory_Road_PO.png" decoding="async" class="thumbimage" srcset="//archives.bulbagarden.net/media/upload/thumb/0/0c/Victory_Road_PO.png/375px-Victory_Road_PO.png 1.5x, //archives.bulbagarden.net/media/upload/thumb/0/0c/Victory_Road_PO.png/500px-Victory_Road_PO.png 2x" width="250" height="141"></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Victory_Road_PO.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Victory Road in <a href="/wiki/Pok%C3%A9mon_Origins" title="Pokémon Origins">Pokémon Origins</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Red_Charizard_Moltres_Flamethrower_PO.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//archives.bulbagarden.net/media/upload/thumb/d/d7/Red_Charizard_Moltres_Flamethrower_PO.png/250px-Red_Charizard_Moltres_Flamethrower_PO.png" decoding="async" class="thumbimage" srcset="//archives.bulbagarden.net/media/upload/thumb/d/d7/Red_Charizard_Moltres_Flamethrower_PO.png/375px-Red_Charizard_Moltres_Flamethrower_PO.png 1.5x, //archives.bulbagarden.net/media/upload/thumb/d/d7/Red_Charizard_Moltres_Flamethrower_PO.png/500px-Red_Charizard_Moltres_Flamethrower_PO.png 2x" width="250" height="141"></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Red_Charizard_Moltres_Flamethrower_PO.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Moltres's nest in Pokémon Origins</div></div></div>
<h3><span id="Pokémon_Origins"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Pok.C3.A9mon_Origins">Pokémon Origins</span></h3>
<p>Victory Road appeared briefly in <i><a href="/wiki/PO04" title="PO04">File 4: Charizard</a></i>, as <a href="/wiki/Red_(Origins)" title="Red (Origins)">Red</a> was shown exiting it on his way to the <a href="/wiki/Indigo_Plateau" title="Indigo Plateau">Indigo Plateau</a>. Later in the episode, Red was shown battling <a href="/wiki/Moltres_(Pok%C3%A9mon)" title="Moltres (Pokémon)">Moltres</a> at the Victory Road with his <a href="/wiki/Red%27s_Charizard" title="Red's Charizard">Charizard</a>, catching the Legendary bird soon after off-screen.
<br clear="all">
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Trivia">Trivia</span></h2>
<ul><li>In <a href="/wiki/Generation_II" title="Generation II">Generations II</a> and <a href="/wiki/Generation_IV" title="Generation IV">IV</a>, Kanto Victory Road has the fewest Trainers of all Victory Roads, the only Trainer battle being against <a href="/wiki/Silver_(game)" title="Silver (game)">Silver</a>.</li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Generation_I" title="Generation I">Generation I</a>, if the player falls through the hole from 3F to 2F while riding their <a href="/wiki/Bicycle" title="Bicycle">bike</a>, they will be forced off the bike in the transition, but the bike music will keep playing.</li></ul>

<script>
// Initialize elements
appendElementIf({id: "adthrive-left-s", wAbove: 1520, wBelow: 1699, hAbove: 700});
appendElementIf({id: "adthrive-left-m", wAbove: 1700, wBelow: 1890, hAbove: 700});
appendElementIf({id: "adthrive-left-l", wAbove: 1891, hAbove: 700});

appendElementIf({id: "adthrive-right-s", wAbove: 945, wBelow: 1099, hAbove: 964});
appendElementIf({id: "adthrive-right-m", wAbove: 1100, wBelow: 1399, hAbove: 964});
appendElementIf({id: "adthrive-right-l", wAbove: 1400, hAbove: 964});
appendElementIf({id: "adthrive-right-rect", hBelow: 964});


// Appends element if condition is met
function appendElementIf({id, wAbove, wBelow, hAbove, hBelow}) {

	// find browser height
	var w = window.innerWidth;
	var h = window.innerHeight;

	// If true after browser size check then unit is added
	var condition = true;

	// Check size conditions
	if (wBelow && (w > wBelow)) condition = false;
	if (wAbove && (w < wAbove)) condition = false;

	if (hBelow && (h > hBelow)) condition = false;
	if (hAbove && (h < hAbove)) condition = false;

	// Append element if condition is met
	if (condition) {
		createAndAppendElement(id);
	}
}


// creates and appends a div element to the body
function createAndAppendElement(id)
{
	var atEl = document.createElement('div');
	atEl.id = id;
	document.body.appendChild(atEl);
}
</script>
